        </div><div class="casAbstract">The electrochem. properties of materials derived from NaTi3O6(OH)·2H2O have been investigated for the first time.  The parent compd. has a corrugated layered structure consisting of {Ti6O14}4- units with hydrated sodium cations and protons in the interlayer spaces.  Upon heating to 600 °C, water is removed irreversibly, the interlayer distances become smaller, and connecting bonds between the octahedral layers form.  It was found that this material can reversibly intercalate both lithium and sodium.  The initial specific discharge capacities, as measured in half-cells, varied with the state of hydration and the nature of the counter electrode (Na or Li).  The electrochem. potential showed a non-linear sloping dependence with degree of intercalation, indicative of a solid-soln. mechanism of intercalation.  The process was centered at a low av. potential of about 0.3 V vs. Na or Li, the lowest ever reported for titanate-based Li hosts.  The higher d. and potential for higher rate capability of this compd., in comparison to carbonaceous materials with similar voltage and reversible capacities, make a compelling case for its development as an anode material, for both lithium and sodium ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref10" class="refNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit10" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2012.10.025"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gotoh, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ishikawa, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shimadzu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yabuuchi, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Komaba, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Takeda, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Goto, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Deguchi, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ohki, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hashi, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shimizu, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ishida, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">NMR study for electrochemically inserted Na in hard carbon electrode of sodium ion battery</span>. <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The state of Na inserted in the hard C electrode of a Na ion battery having practical cyclability was studied using solid state 23Na NMR.  The spectra of C samples charged (reduced) &gt; 50 mAh g-1 showed clear three components.  Two peaks at 9.9 ppm and 5.2 ppm were ascribed to reversible Na stored between disordered graphene sheets in hard C because the shift of the peaks was invariable with changing strength of external magnetic field.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Prussian Blue analogs (PBAs) have shown promise as electrode materials for grid-scale batteries because of their high cycle life and rapid kinetics in aq.-based electrolytes.  However, these materials suffer from relatively low specific capacity, which may limit their practical applications.  Here, we investigate strategies to improve the specific capacity of these materials while maintaining their cycling stability and elucidate mechanisms that enhance their electrochem. properties.  In particular, we have studied the electrochem. and structural properties of manganese hexacyanoferrate (MnHCFe) and cobalt hexacyanoferrate (CoHCFe) in an aq., sodium-ion electrolyte.  We also studied manganese-cobalt hexacyanoferrate (Mn-CoHCFe) solid solns. with different Mn/Co ratios that combine properties of both MnHCFe and CoHCFe.  The materials have the characteristic open-framework crystal structure of PBAs, and their specific capacities can be significantly improved by electrochem. cycling (oxidizing and reducing) both the carbon-coordinated Fe and the nitrogen-coordinated Co or Mn ions.  In situ synchrotron X-ray diffraction studies and ex situ soft X-ray absorption spectroscopy combined with an in-depth electrochem. characterization provide insight into the different electrochem. properties assocd. with the Fe, Co, and Mn redox couples.  We show that cycling the C-coordinated Fe preserves the crystal structure and enables the outstanding kinetics and cycle life previously displayed by PBAs in aq. electrolytes.  On the other hand, the N-coordinated Co and Mn ions exhibit a slower kinetic regime due to structural distortions resulting from the weak N-coordinated crystal field, but they still contribute significantly towards increasing the specific capacity of the materials.  These results provide the understanding needed to drive future development of PBAs for grid-scale applications that require extremely high cycle life and kinetics.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref14" class="refNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit14" data-doi="10.1021/cm101377h"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Moreau, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guyomard, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gaubicher, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Boucher, F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Structure and Stability of Sodium Intercalated Phases in Olivine FePO<sub>4</sub></span>. <i>Chem.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The behavior of a NaFePO4 cathode, obtained by electrochem. Li-Na exchange of LiFePO4 olivine, is characterized in a sodium battery.                         cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Unexpected discovery of low-cost maricite NaFePO4 as a high-performance electrode for Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Jongsoon; Seo, Dong-Hwa; Kim, Hyungsub; Park, Inchul; Yoo, Jung-Keun; Jung, Sung-Kyun; Park, Young-Uk; Goddard, William A., III; Kang, Kisuk</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Battery chem. based on earth-abundant elements has great potential for the development of cost-effective, large-scale energy storage systems.  Herein, we report, for the first time, that maricite NaFePO4 can function as an excellent cathode material for Na ion batteries, an unexpected result since it has been regarded as an electrochem. inactive electrode for rechargeable batteries.  Our investigation of the Na re-(de)intercalation mechanism reveals that all Na ions can be deintercalated from the nano-sized maricite NaFePO4 with simultaneous transformation into amorphous FePO4.  Our quantum mechanics calcns. show that the underlying reason for the remarkable electrochem. activity of NaFePO4 is the significantly enhanced Na mobility in the transformed phase, which is ∼one fourth of the hopping activation barrier.  Maricite NaFePO4, fully sodiated amorphous FePO4, delivered a capacity of 142 mA h g-1 (92% of the theor. value) at the first cycle, and showed outstanding cyclability with a negligible capacity fade after 200 cycles (95% retention of the initial cycle).</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref17" class="refNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit17" data-doi="10.1149/1.3236480"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Recham, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chotard, J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Owing to cost and abundance considerations, Na-based electrode materials are regaining interest, esp. those that can be prepd. at low temps.  The low-temp. synthesis of highly divided Na-based fluorophosphates (Na2MPO4F, M = Fe, Mn, or mixts.) in ionic liq. media is presented.  The ionothermal approach enables the synthesis of these phases at temps. ≥270°, while temps. ≤600°C are needed to obtain similar quality phases by solid-state reactions.  Due to their highly divided character, Na2FePO4F powders made via this process show better electrochem. performances vs. either Li or Na than their ceramic counterparts.  Regardless of how they were made, the Na2MnPO4F powders, which crystallize in a 3-dimensional (3D) tunnel structure rather than in the 2-dimensional (2D)-layered structure of Na2FePO4F, were poorly electroactive.  Substituting 0.25 Fe for Mn in Na2Fe1-xMnxPO4F is sufficient to trigger a 2-dimensional-3D structural transition and leads to rapid decay of the materials electrochem. performances.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Considering the promising electrochem. performance of the recently reported pyrophosphate family in Li ion batteries as well as the increasing importance of Na ion batteries (SIBs) for emerging large-scale applications, here, the crystal structure, electrochem. properties, and thermal stability of Na2FeP2O7, the 1st example ever reported in the pyrophosphate family for SIBs, are studied.  Na2FeP2O7 maintains well-defined channel structures (triclinic framework under the P1 space group) and exhibits a reversible capacity of ≈90 mA-h g-1 with good cycling performance.  Both quasi-equil. measurements and 1st-principles calcns. consistently indicate that Na2FeP2O7 undergoes 2 kinds of reactions over the entire voltage range of 2.0-4.5 V (vs. Na/Na+): a single-phase reaction around 2.5 V and 2-phase reactions in the voltage range of 3.0-3.25 V.  Na2FeP2O7 shows excellent thermal stability up to 500°, even in the partially de-sodiated state (NaFeP2O7), which suggests its safe character, a property that is very crit. for large-scale battery applications.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref22" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201100772"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Barpanda, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nishimura, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yamada, A.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High-Voltage Pyrophosphate Cathodes</span>. <i>Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The quest to explore and to discover novel cathode materials is key to sustaining the progress of Li-ion rechargeable batteries.  It has encouraged materials' chemists to design and develop a variety of polyanionic compds.  This paper reports and summarizes recent progress in the development of alkali metal pyrophosphate based cathode materials for battery applications.  It points out that the pyrophosphate-based polyanionic-framework materials offer a rich crystal chem., ease of synthesis and robust structure offering good alkali-ion mobility.  Thus, they can form a promising class of cathode materials both for lithium- and sodium-ion secondary batteries.  In the Perspectives section, it is speculated that keen study of the myriad of pyrophosphate phases, selective screening and design of key pyrophosphate compds. with open frameworks and optimizing those compds. with nanosizing and carbon coating can lead to breakthroughs in the realization of com. viable high-voltage Li-ion and Na-ion pyrophosphate cathodes.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref23" class="refNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit23" data-doi="10.1002/smtd.201800253"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Senthilkumar, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Murugesan, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sharma, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lochab, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Barpanda, P.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">An Overview of Mixed Polyanionic Cathode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Small Methods.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>3</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1800253</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  "Building better batteries" remains an ongoing process to cater diverse energy demands starting from small-scale consumer electronics to large-scale automobiles and grid storage.  While Li-ion batteries have carried this burden over the last three decades, the ever-growing and highly diverse applications (based on size, energy-d., and stationary vs mobile usages) have led to an era of "beyond lithium-ion batteries.  " In this postlithium-battery era, sodium-ion batteries (NIBs) have emerged as a pragmatic option particularly for large-scale applications.  They attract attention due to the abundance and uniform geog. distribution of sodium-based minerals, materials/process economy, and well-known (de)intercalation mechanisms, in particular for stationary applications independent of size/wt. restriction.  Parallel to the Li-ion batteries, the cathode (pos. electrode) plays a key role in overall performance, leading to the exploration of various layered and 3D framework insertion materials.  While layered oxides deliver high capacity, polyanionic hosts offer structural stability, operational safety, and tunable redox potentials.  It can be further exploited in "mixed polyanion" cathode materials combining more than one kind of polyanion units.  This article focuses on mixed polyanionic cathode materials for NIBs.  It renders a sneak-peek on suites of mixed polyanionic insertion materials discussing their structure, overall electrochem. performance, and future perspectives.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref24" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1021/cm001210d"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sanz, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Parada, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rojo, J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">New iron-based mixed-polyanion compds. LixNa4-xFe3(PO4)2(P2O7) (x = 0-3) were synthesized, and their crystal structures were detd.  The new compds. contained three-dimensional sodium/lithium paths supported by P2O7 pillars in the crystal.  First principles calcns. identified the complex three-dimensional paths with their activation barriers and showed them as fast ionic conductors.  The reversible electrode operation was found in both Li and Na cells with capacities of one-electron reaction per Fe atom, 140 and 129 mA-h/g, resp.  The redox potential of each phase was ∼3.4 V (vs. Li) for the Li-ion cell and ∼3.2 V (vs. Na) for the Na-ion cell.  The properties of high power, small vol. change, and high thermal stability were also recognized, presenting this new compd. as a potential competitor to other iron-based electrodes such as Li2FeP2O7, Li2FePO4F, and LiFePO4.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref26" class="refNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit26" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2013.01.162"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nose, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nakayama, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nobuhara, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yamaguchi, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nakanishi, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Iba, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Na<sub>4</sub>Co<sub>3</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>P<sub>2</sub>O<sub>7</sub>: A novel storage material for sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na4Co3(PO4)2P2O7: A novel storage material for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Nose, Masafumi; Nakayama, Hideki; Nobuhara, Kunihiro; Yamaguchi, Hiroyuki; Nakanishi, Shinji; Iba, Hideki</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The electrochem. properties of Na4Co3(PO4)2P2O7 as a pos. electrode for sodium-ion batteries were characterized by a cyclic voltammetry technique and galvanostatic charge/discharge tests.  Interestingly, Na4Co3(PO4)2P2O7 has the multi-redox couples in the highest potential region between 4.1 V and 4.7 V among ever reported sodium storage materials and can deliver the reversible capacity of ∼95 mAhg-1, corresponding to ∼2.2 Na+ extn. and insertion in Na4Co3(PO4)2P2O7, at the c.d. of 34 mAg-1 (0.2 C).  Na4Co3(PO4)2P2O7 also exhibits the high rate capabilities and has a small polarization in the charge-discharge profile even at the high current densities of 4.25 Ag-1 (25 C), resulting in high energy efficiency of the battery.  These performances indicate Na4Co3(PO4)2P2O7 can be a good candidate as a pos. electrode material of sodium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref27" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2016.07.061"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhong, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sol-gel synthesis of Na<sub>4</sub>Fe<sub>3</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>(P<sub>2</sub>O<sub>7</sub>)/C nanocomposite for sodium-ion batteries and new insights into microstructural evolution during sodium extraction</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sol-gel synthesis of Na4Fe3(PO4)2(P2O7)/C nanocomposite for sodium ion batteries and new insights into microstructural evolution during sodium extraction</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Xuehang; Zhong, Guiming; Tang, Zheng; Yang, Yong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">327</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">666-674</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A mixed polyanionic Na4Fe3(PO4)2(P2O7)/C nanocomposite is synthesized via a sol-gel route.  The phosphate raw material is transformed to the mixed phosphate-pyrophosphate with high phase purity via a self-condensation reaction at 500°.  Na4Fe3(PO4)2(P2O7)/C can deliver an initial capacity of 110 mAh g-1 at 0.05C with the av. discharge voltage approaching 3.1 V.  The nanocomposite shows excellent rate capability because of the presence of an in-situ formed 3-D network of carbon.  At 10 C rate, the nanocomposite delivers a discharge capacity of 78 mAh g-1 at 25 mAh °C and 82 mAh g-1 at 55°.  The nanocomposite has a good long-term cycling stability, retaining 89% of the initial discharge capacity after 300 cycles.  In-situ XRD results demonstrate that the sodium insertion/extn. process in Na4Fe3(PO4)2(P2O7) is an imperfect solid-soln. reaction with an obvious local lattice distortion instead of an ideal solid-soln. reaction.  Using a solid-state NMR technique, it is further found that the sodium extn. from the Na1, Na3, and Na4 sites causes an obvious change in local structure.  However, the local structure of Na2 remains unchanged, which may aid the stability of the host structure.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref28" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2016.07.006"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Moriwake, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kuwabara, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fisher, C. J.; Nose, Masafumi; Nakayama, Hideki; Nakanishi, Shinji; Iba, Hideki; Ikuhara, Yuichi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries offer a potential soln. to the problem of limited lithium resources, and the newly developed pos. electrode material Na4Co3(PO4)2P2O7 is attracting significant attention due to its high rate, high capacity, and high voltage compared to other sodium-ion battery materials.  However, details of its electronic structure and its charge/discharge behavior are still uncertain.  Here we report detailed first-principles calcns. of the desodiation behavior of Na4Co3(PO4)2P2O7 using the GGA + U formalism of d. functional theory.  Assuming a stepwise desodiation process, removal of Na down to NaCo3(PO4)2P2O7 is found to be accompanied by oxidn. of Co2+ to Co3+.  Further removal of Na to give Co3(PO4)2P2O7 requires oxidn. of oxygen 2p orbitals in the P2O7 polyhedra instead of Co3+ being oxidized to Co4+.  The holes thus formed are expected to be strongly self-trapped, rendering them immobile at room temp.  At the same time, a large vol. shrinkage is obsd. during this last desodiation step, constricting the Na migration channels.  These two factors may explain the difficulty encountered exptl. in removing all Na from Na4Co3(PO4)2P2O7.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref29" class="refNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit29" data-doi="10.1021/cm4013816"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, I.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, K.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, Y.-U.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lim, H.-D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yoon, W.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Understanding the Electrochemical Mechanism of the New Iron-Based Mixed-Phosphate Na<sub>4</sub>Fe<sub>3</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>(P<sub>2</sub>O<sub>7</sub>) in a Na Rechargeable Battery</span>. <i>Chem.                         cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Understanding the Electrochemical Mechanism of the New Iron-Based Mixed-Phosphate Na4Fe3(PO4)2(P2O7) in a Na Rechargeable Battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Hyungsub; Park, Inchul; Lee, Seongsu; Kim, Hyunchul; Park, Kyu-Young; Park, Young-Uk; Kim, Haegyeom; Kim, Jongsoon; Lim, Hee-Dae; Yoon, Won-Sub; Kang, Kisuk</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Compds. with a mixed polyanion framework have recently gained attention as a new class of compds. for material exploration.  The potential tunability of the structure by using various combinations of polyanions can potentially lead to a novel cathode.  However, the redox reaction in complex structures often involves complex structural evolutions during the electrochem. reaction, which require careful anal.  The authors studied the electrochem. mechanism of NaxFe3(PO4)2(P2O7) (1 ≤ x ≤ 4), which was recently proposed as a promising mixed-polyanion cathode for Na rechargeable batteries, using 1st principles calcns. and expts.  The de/sodiation of the NaxFe3(PO4)2(P2O7) electrode occurs via a 1-phase reaction with a reversible Fe2+/Fe3+ redox reaction and accompanies an exceptionally small volumetric change of &lt;4%.  Na ion intercalation usually induces a large volumetric change in conventional systems; therefore, this small vol. change is unusual and was attributed to the open framework of polyanion compds. with P2O7 dimers that are capable of rotating and distorting to accommodate the structural change.  Structural robustness was further obsd. at even highly charged states at temps. ≤530° from in situ XRD and DSC.  Probably the improved understanding of the electrochem. mechanism provided here will expedite the optimization of the new Na4Fe3(PO4)2(P2O7) electrode for Na rechargeable batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref30" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1002/admi.201900805"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Moitzheim, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Put, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Vereecken, P. B.; Barpanda, P.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Colloid and Interface Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">514</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion thin-film micro-batteries form a niche sector of energy storage devices.  Sodium titanate, Na2Ti6O13 (NTO) thin films were deposited by pulsed laser deposition (PLD) using solid-state synthesized polycryst. Na2Ti6O13 compd.  The phase-purity and crystallinity of NTO in bulk and thin-film forms were confirmed by Rietveld refinement.  Electron microscopy and at. force microscopy revealed the formation of uniform ∼100 nm thin film with roughness of ∼4 nm consisting of homogeneous nanoscale grains.  These PLD-deposited NTO thin-films, when tested in Na-half cell architecture, delivered a near theor. reversible capacity close to 42 mA h g-1 involving Ti4+/Ti3+ redox activity along with good cycling stability and rate kinetics.  Na2Ti6O13 can work as an efficient and safe anode in designing sodium-ion thin-film micro-batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref33" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1039/C6CC00065G"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Superior high-rate capability of Na<sub>3</sub>(VO<sub>0.5</sub>)<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>2</sub> nanoparticles embedded in porous graphene through the pseudocapacitive effect</span>. <i>Chem. Commun</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>52</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">3653</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">3656</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C6CC00065G</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D52%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D3653-3656%26journal%3DChem.%2BCommun%26author%3DX.%2BXiang%26author%3DQ.%2BLu%26author%3DM.%2BHan%26author%3DJ.%2BChen%26title%3DSuperior%2Bhigh-rate%2Bcapability%2Bof%2BNa3%2528VO0.5%25292%2528PO4%25292F2%2Bnanoparticles%2Bembedded%2Bin%2Bporous%2Bgraphene%2Bthrough%2Bthe%2Bpseudocapacitive%2Beffect%26doi%3D10.1039%252FC6CC00065G&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsomega.9b03835&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FC6CC00065G&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Superior high-rate capability of Na3(VO0.5)2(PO4)2F2 nanoparticles embedded in porous graphene through the pseudocapacitive effect</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xiang, Xingde; Lu, Qiongqiong; Han, Mo; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Communications (Cambridge, United Kingdom)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">52</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">18</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3653-3656</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CHCOFS</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1359-7345</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na3(VO0.5)2(PO4)2F2 nanoparticles embedded in porous graphene were reported as a superior high-rate cathode material for sodium-ion batteries, exhibiting an excellent electrochem. performance with a high reversible capacity of 100 mA h g-1 at 1 C, 77 mA h g-1 at 50 C, and a capacity retention of 73% after 1000 cycles at 50 C.  In particular, a significant contribution of the pseudocapacitive effect to the Na-storage capacity has been found for the first time.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li></ol></div><script type="text/javascript" nonce="9318ade04c4788d3-SJC">window.refViewer={'ref1':['cit1'],'ref2':['cit2'],'ref3':['cit3'],'ref4':['cit4'],'ref5':['cit5'],'ref6':['cit6'],'ref7':['cit7'],'ref8':['cit8'],'ref9':['cit9'],'ref10':['cit10'],'ref11':['cit11'],'ref12':['cit12'],'ref13':['cit13'],'ref14':['cit14'],'ref15':['cit15'],'ref16':['cit16'],'ref17':['cit17'],'ref18':['cit18'],'ref19':['cit19'],'ref20':['cit20'],'ref21':['cit21'],'ref22':['cit22'],'ref23':['cit23'],'ref24':['cit24'],'ref25':['cit25'],'ref26':['cit26'],'ref27':['cit27'],'ref28':['cit28'],'ref29':['cit29'],'ref30':['cit30'],'ref31':['cit31'],'ref32':['cit32'],'ref33':['cit33']}</script><div class="articleCitedByDropzone" data-pb-dropzone="articleCitedByDropzone"><div class="cited-by"><div class="article_content-header cited-content_header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div tabindex="0" class="article_content-title"><h2 id="citeThis">Cited By</h2><div class="article__copy"> <button class="article__copy__btn"><i aria-hidden="true" class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><div class="cited-by__content"><div class="sciteMetricsDropzone">

Future outlook of sodium-ion batteries is discussed.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201200026"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, S. W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Seo, D. H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ceder, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrode Materials for Rechargeable Sodium-Ion Batteries: Potential Alternatives to Current Lithium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv. Energy Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2012</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>2</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">710</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">721</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/aenm.201200026</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrode materials for rechargeable sodium-ion batteries: potential alternatives to current lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Sung-Wook; Seo, Dong-Hwa; Ma, Xiaohua; Ceder, Gerbrand; Kang, Kisuk</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">710-721</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADEMBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1614-6840</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Lithium (Li)-ion batteries (LIB) have governed the current worldwide rechargeable battery market due to their outstanding energy and power capability.  In particular, the LIB's role in enabling elec. vehicles (EVs) has been highlighted to replace the current oil-driven vehicles in order to reduce the usage of oil resources and generation of CO2 gases.  Unlike Li, sodium is one of the more abundant elements on Earth and exhibits similar chem. properties to Li, indicating that Na chem. could be applied to a similar battery system.  In the 1970s-80s, both Na-ion and Li-ion electrodes were investigated, but the higher energy d. of Li-ion cells made them more applicable to small, portable electronic devices, and research efforts for rechargeable batteries have been mainly concd. on LIB since then.  Recently, research interest in Na-ion batteries (NIB) has been resurrected, driven by new applications with requirements different from those in portable electronics, and to address the concern on Li abundance.  In this article, both neg. and pos. electrode materials in NIB are briefly reviewed.  While the voltage is generally lower and the vol. change upon Na removal or insertion is larger for Na-intercalation electrodes, compared to their Li equiv., the power capability can vary depending on the crystal structures.  It is concluded that cost-effective NIB can partially replace LIB, but requires further investigation and improvement.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref3" class="rightTabRefNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit3" data-doi="10.1039/C6CS00776G"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hwang, J. Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Myung, S. T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y. K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sodium-ion batteries: present and future</span>. <i>Chem. Soc. Rev.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>46</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">3529</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">3614</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C6CS00776G</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium-ion batteries: present and future</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hwang, Jang-Yeon; Myung, Seung-Taek; Sun, Yang-Kook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Society Reviews</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">46</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3529-3614</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CSRVBR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0306-0012</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Energy prodn. and storage technologies have attracted a great deal of attention for day-to-day applications.  In recent decades, advances in lithium-ion battery (LIB) technol. have improved living conditions around the globe.  LIBs are used in most mobile electronic devices as well as in zero-emission electronic vehicles.  However, there are increasing concerns regarding load leveling of renewable energy sources and the smart grid as well as the sustainability of lithium sources due to their limited availability and consequent expected price increase.  Therefore, whether LIBs alone can satisfy the rising demand for small- and/or mid-to-large-format energy storage applications remains unclear.  To mitigate these issues, recent research has focused on alternative energy storage systems.  Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered as the best candidate power sources because sodium is widely available and exhibits similar chem. to that of LIBs; therefore, SIBs are promising next-generation alternatives.  Recently, sodiated layer transition metal oxides, phosphates and org. compds. have been introduced as cathode materials for SIBs.  Simultaneously, recent developments have been facilitated by the use of select carbonaceous materials, transition metal oxides (or sulfides), and intermetallic and org. compds. as anodes for SIBs.  Apart from electrode materials, suitable electrolytes, additives, and binders are equally important for the development of practical SIBs.  Despite developments in electrode materials and other components, there remain several challenges, including cell design and electrode balancing, in the application of sodium ion cells.  In this article, we summarize and discuss current research on materials and propose future directions for SIBs.  This will provide important insights into scientific and practical issues in the development of SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref4" class="rightTabRefNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit4" data-doi="10.1039/C4EE03192J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, M. H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gonzalo, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Singh, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rojo, T.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A comprehensive review of sodium layered oxides: powerful cathodes for Na-ion batteries</span>. <i>Energy Environ. Sci.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>8</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">81</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">102</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C4EE03192J</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A comprehensive review of sodium layered oxides: powerful cathodes for Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Han, Man Huon; Gonzalo, Elena; Singh, Gurpreet; Rojo, Teofilo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">81-102</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The room temp. Na-ion secondary battery has been under focus lately due to its feasibility to compete against the already well-established Li-ion secondary battery.  Although there are many obstacles to overcome before the Na-ion battery becomes com. available, recent research discoveries corroborate that some of the cathode materials for the Na-ion battery have indeed indisputable advantages over its Li-ion counterparts.  In this publication, a comprehensive review of layered oxides (NaTMO2, TM = Ti, V, Cr, Mn, Fe, Co, Ni, and a mixt. of 2 or 3 elements) as a viable Na-ion battery cathode is presented.  Single TM systems are well characterized not only for their electrochem. performance but also for their structural transitions during the cycle.  Binary TM systems are investigated in order to address issues regarding low reversible capacity, capacity retention, operating voltage, and structural stability.  As a consequence, some materials already have reached an energy d. of 520 mW h g-1, which is comparable to that of LiFePO4.  Furthermore, some ternary TM systems retained more than 72% of their capacity along with over 99.7% Coulombic efficiency for 275 cycles.  The goal of this review is to present the development of Na layered oxide materials in the past as well as the state of the art today in order to emphasize the compatibility and durability of layered oxides as powerful candidates for Na-ion battery cathode materials.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref5" class="rightTabRefNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit5" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201703055"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Barpanda, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lander, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nishimura, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yamada, A.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Polyanionic Insertion Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A layered phase, NaNi1/3Mn1/3Co1/3O2 (NaNMC), isostructural with NaCoO2, was synthesized.  Stoichiometric NaNMC crystallizes in a rhombohedral R3-m space group where Na is in an octahedral environment (O3-Type).  Galvanostatic cycling on NaNMC vs. Na cell indicated a reversible intercalation of 0.5 Na, leading to a capacity of 120 mA-h/g in the voltage range of 2-3.75 V and indicating its possible application in Na-ion batteries.  The electrochem. driven Na insertion/de-insertion in NaNMC is assocd. with several phase transitions and solid soln. regimes which are studied by in situ XRD.  Na de-insertion in NaxNMC resulted in sequential phase transitions composed of biphasic and monophasic domains.  The compn. driven structural evolution in NaxNMC follows the sequence O3 → O1 → P3 → P1 phases with an increased 'c' parameter, while the 'a' parameter remains almost unchanged.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref7" class="rightTabRefNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit7" data-doi="10.1038/nmat3309"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yabuuchi, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kajiyama, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Iwatate, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nishikawa, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hitomi, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Okuyama, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Usui, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yamada, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Komaba, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">P2-type Na<i><sub>x</sub></i>[Fe<sub>1/2</sub>Mn<sub>1/2</sub>]O<sub>2</sub> made from earth-abundant elements for rechargeable Na batteries</span>. <i>Nat.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Rechargeable Li batteries have risen to prominence as key devices for green and sustainable energy development.  Mn- and Fe-based cathode materials, such as LiMn2O4 and LiFePO4, are used in large-scale batteries for elec. vehicles.  Mn and Fe are abundant elements in the Earth's crust, but Li is not.  In contrast to Li, Na is an attractive charge carrier from elemental abundance.  Recently, some layered materials, where Na can be electrochem. and reversibly extd./inserted, have been reported.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The electrochem. properties of materials derived from NaTi3O6(OH)·2H2O have been investigated for the first time.  The parent compd. has a corrugated layered structure consisting of {Ti6O14}4- units with hydrated sodium cations and protons in the interlayer spaces.  Upon heating to 600 °C, water is removed irreversibly, the interlayer distances become smaller, and connecting bonds between the octahedral layers form.  It was found that this material can reversibly intercalate both lithium and sodium.  The initial specific discharge capacities, as measured in half-cells, varied with the state of hydration and the nature of the counter electrode (Na or Li).  The electrochem. potential showed a non-linear sloping dependence with degree of intercalation, indicative of a solid-soln. mechanism of intercalation.  The process was centered at a low av. potential of about 0.3 V vs. Na or Li, the lowest ever reported for titanate-based Li hosts. Andrew; Yang, Wanli; Toney, Michael F.; Cui, Yi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Prussian Blue analogs (PBAs) have shown promise as electrode materials for grid-scale batteries because of their high cycle life and rapid kinetics in aq.-based electrolytes.  However, these materials suffer from relatively low specific capacity, which may limit their practical applications.  Here, we investigate strategies to improve the specific capacity of these materials while maintaining their cycling stability and elucidate mechanisms that enhance their electrochem. properties.  In particular, we have studied the electrochem. and structural properties of manganese hexacyanoferrate (MnHCFe) and cobalt hexacyanoferrate (CoHCFe) in an aq., sodium-ion electrolyte.  We also studied manganese-cobalt hexacyanoferrate (Mn-CoHCFe) solid solns. with different Mn/Co ratios that combine properties of both MnHCFe and CoHCFe.  The materials have the characteristic open-framework crystal structure of PBAs, and their specific capacities can be significantly improved by electrochem. cycling (oxidizing and reducing) both the carbon-coordinated Fe and the nitrogen-coordinated Co or Mn ions.  In situ synchrotron X-ray diffraction studies and ex situ soft X-ray absorption spectroscopy combined with an in-depth electrochem. characterization provide insight into the different electrochem. properties assocd. with the Fe, Co, and Mn redox couples.  We show that cycling the C-coordinated Fe preserves the crystal structure and enables the outstanding kinetics and cycle life previously displayed by PBAs in aq. electrolytes.  On the other hand, the N-coordinated Co and Mn ions exhibit a slower kinetic regime due to structural distortions resulting from the weak N-coordinated crystal field, but they still contribute significantly towards increasing the specific capacity of the materials.  These results provide the understanding needed to drive future development of PBAs for grid-scale applications that require extremely high cycle life and kinetics.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref14" class="rightTabRefNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit14" data-doi="10.1021/cm101377h"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Moreau, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guyomard, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gaubicher, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Boucher, F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Structure and Stability of Sodium Intercalated Phases in Olivine FePO<sub>4</sub></span>. <i>Chem. Herein, we report, for the first time, that maricite NaFePO4 can function as an excellent cathode material for Na ion batteries, an unexpected result since it has been regarded as an electrochem. inactive electrode for rechargeable batteries.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Considering the promising electrochem. performance of the recently reported pyrophosphate family in Li ion batteries as well as the increasing importance of Na ion batteries (SIBs) for emerging large-scale applications, here, the crystal structure, electrochem. properties, and thermal stability of Na2FeP2O7, the 1st example ever reported in the pyrophosphate family for SIBs, are studied.  Na2FeP2O7 maintains well-defined channel structures (triclinic framework under the P1 space group) and exhibits a reversible capacity of ≈90 mA-h g-1 with good cycling performance.  Both quasi-equil. measurements and 1st-principles calcns. consistently indicate that Na2FeP2O7 undergoes 2 kinds of reactions over the entire voltage range of 2.0-4.5 V (vs. Na/Na+): a single-phase reaction around 2.5 V and 2-phase reactions in the voltage range of 3.0-3.25 V.  Na2FeP2O7 shows excellent thermal stability up to 500°, even in the partially de-sodiated state (NaFeP2O7), which suggests its safe character, a property that is very crit. for large-scale battery applications.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref22" class="rightTabRefNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit22" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201100772"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Barpanda, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nishimura, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yamada, A.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High-Voltage Pyrophosphate Cathodes</span>. <i>Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The quest to explore and to discover novel cathode materials is key to sustaining the progress of Li-ion rechargeable batteries.  It has encouraged materials' chemists to design and develop a variety of polyanionic compds.  This paper reports and summarizes recent progress in the development of alkali metal pyrophosphate based cathode materials for battery applications.  It points out that the pyrophosphate-based polyanionic-framework materials offer a rich crystal chem., ease of synthesis and robust structure offering good alkali-ion mobility.  Thus, they can form a promising class of cathode materials both for lithium- and sodium-ion secondary batteries.  In the Perspectives section, it is speculated that keen study of the myriad of pyrophosphate phases, selective screening and design of key pyrophosphate compds. with open frameworks and optimizing those compds. with nanosizing and carbon coating can lead to breakthroughs in the realization of com. viable high-voltage Li-ion and Na-ion pyrophosphate cathodes.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref23" class="rightTabRefNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit23" data-doi="10.1002/smtd.201800253"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Senthilkumar, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Murugesan, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sharma, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lochab, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Barpanda, P.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">An Overview of Mixed Polyanionic Cathode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Small Methods.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>3</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1800253</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  "Building better batteries" remains an ongoing process to cater diverse energy demands starting from small-scale consumer electronics to large-scale automobiles and grid storage.  While Li-ion batteries have carried this burden over the last three decades, the ever-growing and highly diverse applications (based on size, energy-d., and stationary vs mobile usages) have led to an era of "beyond lithium-ion batteries.  " In this postlithium-battery era, sodium-ion batteries (NIBs) have emerged as a pragmatic option particularly for large-scale applications.  They attract attention due to the abundance and uniform geog. distribution of sodium-based minerals, materials/process economy, and well-known (de)intercalation mechanisms, in particular for stationary applications independent of size/wt. restriction.  Parallel to the Li-ion batteries, the cathode (pos. electrode) plays a key role in overall performance, leading to the exploration of various layered and 3D framework insertion materials.  While layered oxides deliver high capacity, polyanionic hosts offer structural stability, operational safety, and tunable redox potentials.  It can be further exploited in "mixed polyanion" cathode materials combining more than one kind of polyanion units.  This article focuses on mixed polyanionic cathode materials for NIBs.  It renders a sneak-peek on suites of mixed polyanionic insertion materials discussing their structure, overall electrochem. performance, and future perspectives.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref24" class="rightTabRefNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit24" data-doi="10.1021/cm001210d"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sanz, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Parada, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rojo, J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A mixed polyanionic Na4Fe3(PO4)2(P2O7)/C nanocomposite is synthesized via a sol-gel route.  The phosphate raw material is transformed to the mixed phosphate-pyrophosphate with high phase purity via a self-condensation reaction at 500°.  Na4Fe3(PO4)2(P2O7)/C can deliver an initial capacity of 110 mAh g-1 at 0.05C with the av. discharge voltage approaching 3.1 V.  The nanocomposite shows excellent rate capability because of the presence of an in-situ formed 3-D network of carbon.  At 10 C rate, the nanocomposite delivers a discharge capacity of 78 mAh g-1 at 25 mAh °C and 82 mAh g-1 at 55°.  The nanocomposite has a good long-term cycling stability, retaining 89% of the initial discharge capacity after 300 cycles.  In-situ XRD results demonstrate that the sodium insertion/extn. process in Na4Fe3(PO4)2(P2O7) is an imperfect solid-soln. reaction with an obvious local lattice distortion instead of an ideal solid-soln. reaction.  Using a solid-state NMR technique, it is further found that the sodium extn. from the Na1, Na3, and Na4 sites causes an obvious change in local structure. Power Sources</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>326</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">220</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">225</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.jpowsour.2016.07.006</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Crystal and electronic structure changes during the charge-discharge process of Na4Co3(PO4)2P2O7</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Moriwake, Hiroki; Kuwabara, Akihide; Fisher, Craig A. J.; Nose, Masafumi; Nakayama, Hideki; Nakanishi, Shinji; Iba, Hideki; Ikuhara, Yuichi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">326</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">220-225</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries offer a potential soln. to the problem of limited lithium resources, and the newly developed pos. electrode material Na4Co3(PO4)2P2O7 is attracting significant attention due to its high rate, high capacity, and high voltage compared to other sodium-ion battery materials.  However, details of its electronic structure and its charge/discharge behavior are still uncertain.  Here we report detailed first-principles calcns. of the desodiation behavior of Na4Co3(PO4)2P2O7 using the GGA + U formalism of d. functional theory.  Assuming a stepwise desodiation process, removal of Na down to NaCo3(PO4)2P2O7 is found to be accompanied by oxidn. of Co2+ to Co3+.  Further removal of Na to give Co3(PO4)2P2O7 requires oxidn. of oxygen 2p orbitals in the P2O7 polyhedra instead of Co3+ being oxidized to Co4+.  The holes thus formed are expected to be strongly self-trapped, rendering them immobile at room temp.  At the same time, a large vol. shrinkage is obsd. during this last desodiation step, constricting the Na migration channels.  These two factors may explain the difficulty encountered exptl. in removing all Na from Na4Co3(PO4)2P2O7.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref29" class="rightTabRefNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit29" data-doi="10.1021/cm4013816"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, I.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, K.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, Y.-U.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lim, H.-D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yoon, W.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Understanding the Electrochemical Mechanism of the New Iron-Based Mixed-Phosphate Na<sub>4</sub>Fe<sub>3</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>(P<sub>2</sub>O<sub>7</sub>) in a Na Rechargeable Battery</span>. <i>Chem. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>25</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">3614</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">3622</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/cm4013816</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Understanding the Electrochemical Mechanism of the New Iron-Based Mixed-Phosphate Na4Fe3(PO4)2(P2O7) in a Na Rechargeable Battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Hyungsub; Park, Inchul; Lee, Seongsu; Kim, Hyunchul; Park, Kyu-Young; Park, Young-Uk; Kim, Haegyeom; Kim, Jongsoon; Lim, Hee-Dae; Yoon, Won-Sub; Kang, Kisuk</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">25</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">18</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3614-3622</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMATEX</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0897-4756</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Compds. with a mixed polyanion framework have recently gained attention as a new class of compds. for material exploration.  The potential tunability of the structure by using various combinations of polyanions can potentially lead to a novel cathode.  However, the redox reaction in complex structures often involves complex structural evolutions during the electrochem. reaction, which require careful anal.  The authors studied the electrochem. mechanism of NaxFe3(PO4)2(P2O7) (1 ≤ x ≤ 4), which was recently proposed as a promising mixed-polyanion cathode for Na rechargeable batteries, using 1st principles calcns. and expts.  The de/sodiation of the NaxFe3(PO4)2(P2O7) electrode occurs via a 1-phase reaction with a reversible Fe2+/Fe3+ redox reaction and accompanies an exceptionally small volumetric change of &lt;4%.  Na ion intercalation usually induces a large volumetric change in conventional systems; therefore, this small vol. change is unusual and was attributed to the open framework of polyanion compds. with P2O7 dimers that are capable of rotating and distorting to accommodate the structural change.  Structural robustness was further obsd. at even highly charged states at temps. ≤530° from in situ XRD and DSC.  Probably the improved understanding of the electrochem. mechanism provided here will expedite the optimization of the new Na4Fe3(PO4)2(P2O7) electrode for Na rechargeable batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref30" class="rightTabRefNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit30" data-doi="10.1002/admi.201900805"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Moitzheim, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Put, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Vereecken, P. M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Advances in 3D Thin-Film Li-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv. Mater. Interfaces.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>6</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1900805</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/admi.201900805</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            rightTab-cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref31" class="rightTabRefNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit31" data-doi="10.16943/ptinsa/2018/49472"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rambabu, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Krupanidhi, S. B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Barpanda, P.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">An Overview of Nanostructured Li-based Thin Film Micro-batteries</span>. <i>Proc. Indian Natl. Sci. Acad.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>98</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">121</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">142</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.16943/ptinsa/2018/49472</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            rightTab-cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref32" class="rightTabRefNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit32" data-doi="10.1016/j.jcis.2017.12.023"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rambabu, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Senthilkumar, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sada, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Krupanidhi, S. B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Barpanda, P.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">In-situ deposition of sodium titanate thin film as anode for sodium-ion micro-batteries developed by pulsed laser deposition</span>. <i>J. Colloid Interface Sci.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>514</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">117</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">121</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.jcis.2017.12.023</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">In-situ deposition of sodium titanate thin film as anode for sodium-ion micro-batteries developed by pulsed laser deposition</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Rambabu, A.; Senthilkumar, B.; Sada, K.; Krupanidhi, S. B.; Barpanda, P.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Colloid and Interface Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">514</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">117-121</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JCISA5</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0021-9797</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion thin-film micro-batteries form a niche sector of energy storage devices.  Sodium titanate, Na2Ti6O13 (NTO) thin films were deposited by pulsed laser deposition (PLD) using solid-state synthesized polycryst. Na2Ti6O13 compd.  The phase-purity and crystallinity of NTO in bulk and thin-film forms were confirmed by Rietveld refinement.  Electron microscopy and at. force microscopy revealed the formation of uniform ∼100 nm thin film with roughness of ∼4 nm consisting of homogeneous nanoscale grains.  These PLD-deposited NTO thin-films, when tested in Na-half cell architecture, delivered a near theor. reversible capacity close to 42 mA h g-1 involving Ti4+/Ti3+ redox activity along with good cycling stability and rate kinetics.  Na2Ti6O13 can work as an efficient and safe anode in designing sodium-ion thin-film micro-batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref33" class="rightTabRefNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit33" data-doi="10.1039/C6CC00065G"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Superior high-rate capability of Na<sub>3</sub>(VO<sub>0.5</sub>)<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>2</sub> nanoparticles embedded in porous graphene through the pseudocapacitive effect</span>. <i>Chem. Commun</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>52</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">3653</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">3656</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C6CC00065G</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Superior high-rate capability of Na3(VO0.5)2(PO4)2F2 nanoparticles embedded in porous graphene through the pseudocapacitive effect</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xiang, Xingde; Lu, Qiongqiong; Han, Mo; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Communications (Cambridge, United Kingdom)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">52</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">18</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3653-3656</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CHCOFS</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1359-7345</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na3(VO0.5)2(PO4)2F2 nanoparticles embedded in porous graphene were reported as a superior high-rate cathode material for sodium-ion batteries, exhibiting an excellent electrochem. performance with a high reversible capacity of 100 mA h g-1 at 1 C, 77 mA h g-1 at 50 C, and a capacity retention of 73% after 1000 cycles at 50 C.  In particular, a significant contribution of the pseudocapacitive effect to the Na-storage capacity has been found for the first time.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li></ol></li><li id="pane-m3" aria-labelledby="pane-m3" class="tab__pane tab__pane-suppInfo"><h2 class="supp-info-label">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article_supporting-info" id="rightTab-notes3"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="rightTab-_i9">Supporting Information</h2></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge at <a href="/doi/10.1021/acsomega.9b03835?goto=supporting-info" class="ext-link">https://pubs.acs.org/doi/10.1021/acsomega.9b03835</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">EDS spectrum, SEM image, elemental mapping images of the Na<sub>4</sub>Fe<sub>3</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>P<sub>2</sub>O<sub>7</sub> powder sample, EDS analysis results table, and the Coulombic efficiency plot (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsomega.9b03835/suppl_file/ao9b03835_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a>)</p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsomega.9b03835/suppl_file/ao9b03835_si_001.pdf">ao9b03835_si_001.pdf (310.73 kb)</a></li></ul></div></div><div id="rightTab-figshare-widget"></div><br><div class="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight" data-pb-dropzone="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight"><div data-widget-def="UX3HTMLWidget" data-widget-id="b84e6b6c-b4d0-4427-b286-3cf14d52d013" class="mb-4">

(function(){

	$('.cit-download-dropdown_button').on('click',function(e)

	    gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':'Main'});

	});

	{

	    var idx = $(this).index();
	    
	    var label = '';
	    if (idx === 0 ) {
	    	label = 'Citation';
	    } else if (idx === 1 ) {
	    	label = 'Abstract';
	    } else if (idx === 2 ) {
	    	label = 'Reference';
	    } else if (idx === 3 ) {
	    	label = 'More Options';
	    }
	   
	   gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':label});
	});

<script nonce="9318ade04c4788d3-SJC">
document.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', function () {
    const modalContainer = document.querySelector('.my-main-container');

    // Function to show the modal
    function showModal() {
        modalContainer.style.display = 'flex';
        document.querySelector('.overlay').style.display = 'block';
    }

    // Function to hide the modal when the close button is clicked
    function hideModal() {
        modalContainer.style.display = 'none';
        document.querySelector('.overlay').style.display = 'none';
    }

    // Hide the modal initially
    hideModal();

    // Function to handle clicks outside the modal
    function handleClickOutside(event) {
        // const modalContainer = document.querySelector(".my-main-container");
        // Check if the click target is not a child of the modal container
        if (!modalContainer.contains(event.target)) {
            hideModal();
        }
    }

    // Add a click event listener to the close button
    document
        .querySelector('.close-button')
        .addEventListener('click', hideModal);

    // Add a click event listener to the document to handle clicks outside the modal
    document.addEventListener('click', handleClickOutside);

    const screenHeight = window.innerHeight;
    function updateModalPosition() {
        const scrollY = window.scrollY;
        // console.log("scrollY= " + scrollY);
        // modalContainer.style.top = `${50 + scrollY}px`;
        modalContainer.style.top = `${scrollY + screenHeight / 2}px`;
        // console.log("new top= " + modalContainer.style.top);
    }

    // Update the modal position when the user scrolls
    window.addEventListener('scroll', updateModalPosition);

    // Initialize the modal position
    updateModalPosition();

    //---Cookie---
    // Function to set the cookie with a given name, value, and expiration time in days
    function setCookie(name, value, days) {
        var expires = '';
        if (days) {
            var date = new Date();
            date.setTime(date.getTime() + days * 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000);
            expires = '; expires=' + date.toUTCString();
            console.log(expires + 'this is expires dateUTC');
        }
        document.cookie = name + '=' + (value || '') + expires + '; path=/';
        // console.log("document.cookie is: " + document.cookie);
    }

    if (!document.cookie.includes('modalAd')) {
        // Show Modal
        showModal();

        // Set the cookie with the name "modalAd", value "true", and expiration of 3 day
        setCookie('modalAd', 'true', 3);
    } else {
        hideModal();
    }
});

</script>
<link rel="stylesheet" type="text/css" href="/pb-assets/smartgroup_ads/Modal-LeadGen-1691422642793.css">
            
        </div>
